  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_25747742-7779-4a37-94e7-32d4b6e07e69'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer12162763392454020522">Delia Hopkins has led a charmed life. Raised in rural New Hampshire by her widowed father, Andrew, she now has a young daughter, a handsome fiance, and her own search-and-rescue bloodhound, which she uses to find missing persons. But as Delia plans her wedding, she is plagued by flashbacks of a life she can't recall. And then a policeman knocks on her door, revealing a sec</span>
  <span id="freeText12162763392454020522" style="display:none">Delia Hopkins has led a charmed life. Raised in rural New Hampshire by her widowed father, Andrew, she now has a young daughter, a handsome fiance, and her own search-and-rescue bloodhound, which she uses to find missing persons. But as Delia plans her wedding, she is plagued by flashbacks of a life she can't recall. And then a policeman knocks on her door, revealing a secret that changes the world as she knows it." In shock and confusion, Delia must sift through the truth - even when it jeopardizes her life and the lives of those she loves. What happens when you learn you are not who you thought you were? When the people you've loved and trusted suddenly change before your eyes? When getting your deepest wish means giving up what you've always taken for granted? Vanishing Acts explores how life - as we know it - might not turn out the way we imagined; how doing the right thing could mean doing the wrong thing; how the memory we thought had vanished could return as a threat.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12162763392454020522" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1000264-what-the-elise-says-on-the-witness">What the???? Elise says on the witness stand that she is 47 years old. Her daughter Delia is 32. She was 15 years old when she gave birth to Delia? Why wasn&#39;t a bigger deal made of the fact that she was a teenager when she had her daughter? And how could she have been working as a bartender at the time? I must have read this wrong.........(?)</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1000264'><a id="like_count_community_question_1000264" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1000264?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">5 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F14865.Vanishing_Acts">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/25558172-vivian"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1533437038i/25558172._UX100_CR0,22,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/25558172-vivian">Vivian</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Charles/Andrew was 33 when he kidnapped Bethany/Delia, so he would've been 29 when Bethany/Delia was conceived. Age of consent in most states is 16, b<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Charles/Andrew was 33 when he kidnapped Bethany/Delia, so he would've been 29 when Bethany/Delia was conceived. Age of consent in most states is 16, but it's 18 in Arizona (I'm assuming that's where Bethany/Delia was conceived). So she's the product of statutory rape. I think the author just didn't do the math right.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    The mother was an alcoholic, having an affair with a man that the father happen to see with his four year old daughter on his lap, while the mother wa<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    The mother was an alcoholic, having an affair with a man that the father happen to see with his four year old daughter on his lap, while the mother was passed out, and in his gut felt the man was abusing her. He had no proof but when he was on a visit with the little girl, she said, "daddy, please don't take me home" and he never looked back.<br /><br /><a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>

<div id="review_19376712" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/19376712" />
    <a title="Jen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/236648-jen"><img alt="Jen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1282693240p2/236648.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/19376712?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen" href="/user/show/236648-jen">Jen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/236648-jen?shelf=z-2008-read">z-2008-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/236648-jen?shelf=ugh">ugh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/236648-jen?shelf=abandoned-ship">abandoned-ship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/236648-jen?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/236648-jen?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer19376712" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15400319030310699378">I'd never read any Jodi Picoult before. I read the first 100 or so pages of this one and didn't want to read any more. I found it very uneven, and the character of Delia just ran around being shrill, unreasonable, and oblivious, while there are three men in her life who seem to live only to please her. Jeez. <br/><br/>Also, I could tell the answer to the "mystery" of why the father did what he did was going to be a long time coming--there seemed to be a lot of secrets conveniently being kept, which I thin</span>
  <span id="freeText15400319030310699378" style="display:none">I'd never read any Jodi Picoult before. I read the first 100 or so pages of this one and didn't want to read any more. I found it very uneven, and the character of Delia just ran around being shrill, unreasonable, and oblivious, while there are three men in her life who seem to live only to please her. Jeez. <br /><br />Also, I could tell the answer to the "mystery" of why the father did what he did was going to be a long time coming--there seemed to be a lot of secrets conveniently being kept, which I think really just served to draw the story out and keep the reader interested along the way. And at 419 pages, that's a long way to go. I was curious enough to find out the "why" of the mystery, so I read the ending and leafed thru a few middle bits. I don't feel like I missed anything.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15400319030310699378" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_443968915" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/443968915" />
    <a title="Teri Zipf" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4753154-teri-zipf"><img alt="Teri Zipf" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1394248463p2/4753154.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/443968915?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Teri Zipf" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Teri Zipf" href="/user/show/4753154-teri-zipf">Teri Zipf</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer443968915&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer443968915" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16997123719356770551">Never reading Jodi Picoult again. If there were just one thing wrong with this book I'd give her another try, but read on. <br/><br/>The number one thing I hated about this book was the Hopi character who has breast cancer and kills herself, without bothering to get any treatment, just jumps off a cliff in front of Delia, who doesn't stop her because if she had to look forward to losing her hair and a breast, she'd probably do it too. Well good god, hair grows back. They can give you new, bigger boobs. Bu</span>
  <span id="freeText16997123719356770551" style="display:none">Never reading Jodi Picoult again. If there were just one thing wrong with this book I'd give her another try, but read on. <br /><br />The number one thing I hated about this book was the Hopi character who has breast cancer and kills herself, without bothering to get any treatment, just jumps off a cliff in front of Delia, who doesn't stop her because if she had to look forward to losing her hair and a breast, she'd probably do it too. Well good god, hair grows back. They can give you new, bigger boobs. But no one can restore you to your family and friends. If this woman had had a chance to think this over, if someone had bothered to go to the doctor with her and see what her options are, she might have changed her mind. <br /><br />We're never given enough information for this to have seemed to have been an informed decision. The woman obviously wasn't in any advanced state of cancer, as she hiked out to this remote spot to jump from, and had previously continued every activity of daily living unimpaired. Why Picoult would even want to put this in a book calls her entire brain into question. <br /><br />The number two thing is Dear Daddy. While being held in jail, mind you, not prison, but county jail, Dear Daddy gets involved in a drug ring manufacturing and selling meth, shoots someone in the eye with a staple, makes a gun, hides a bullet, smuggles drugs and more. Oh yeah and holds his best buddy, the Black Guy Who Has to Die, in his arms as he dies. This is all in what seems to have been about 2 months. And yet Dear Daddy is the good guy. The reader is the only one who knows this, which makes you wonder why it's there at all, but still, if that doesn't reflect on Daddy's character, I don't know what it would take. <br /><br />Number 3. Mommy has not had a drink in 26 years, and reaches out to Delia, and yet there's no indication that Delia has the emotional maturity to forgive and establish a relationship. Get over it Delia. <br /><br />Number 4, Delia. Delia has one admirable trait, being a good mom. Which turns out to be just thinking she's a good mom, see below. Other than that, she's a self-centered, self-righteous bitch who never cuts anyone any slack.<br /><br />Number 5. Victor, Mommy's boyfriend, may or may not have molested Delia, and yet even though he took her daughter for a visit WITHOUT ASKING and had her alone for an uncertain amount of time, Delia, Mother of the Year, never follows up on checking whether Victor may have molested her own daughter, nor does she even tell Victor that that taking a kid without asking is not OK.<br /><br />Number 6. Eric, Delia's fiance, also alcoholic, starts drinking while defending Daddy. So, why does Delia insist on him taking the case? He is most emphatically NOT the best man for the case, as he's not a member of the Arizona bar, has never defended anyone on this kind of charge or even any criminal charges that we know of, and has a background that is sure to cause his immense emotional distress in defending Daddy. <br /><br />But Delia doesn't care about Eric, Delia cares about Delia, and it never crosses her mind to hire someone else. This is because Delia lives in a novel and Jodi Picoult has a lot of points to make.<br /><br />Again, even though Eric himself hasn't drunk for 2 years, Jodi Picoult can't leave him alone and let him be a good guy. Like Mommy, he is bad. Oh, not really bad, because like Fitz and her father, Eric's whole world just revolves around Darling Delia, so that makes him OK. But he is someone you have to throw away for the good of your child. So Delia throws him away for Fitz. I mean the good of her child. Who will be scarred by the whole experience. <br /><br />Finally, although Delia is supposed to be a great mother she never gives a thought to how her child might take this throwing over of Eric, her father, for this other dude. This is because both the guys love Delia, and therefore her daughter, and she probably just won't notice the difference.<br /><br />Number 7, Fitz as a character has one characteristic; he's hopelessly in love with Delia. This is enough for both Delia and Picoult. It's also the only thing he ever talks about, and losing his job is apparently so inconsequential that no one even wonders how he and Delia are going to pay the bills when they get back to New Hampshire. Last I heard, search and rescue, Delia's so-called career, is a volunteer gig, not a paying job. No wonder she still lives with Daddy!<br /><br />Fitz is basically just standing around, waiting for Delia to ride off into the sunset with him. That is, once Eric's life is trashed. This switch from love of her life Eric to best friend Fitz takes about a 2 weeks for Delia to justify. Good luck to all of them.<br /><br />Number 8: I could forgive all the writer's workshop flowery writing if that was the only fault of this book, but it's not. This book in no way stands up to the oh-so-beautiful writing. All the freaking metaphors while the lovemaking characters who are 5 minutes from breaking up was enough to make you puke. Pull a curtain over it gentle writer, and move on. <br /><br />This is a really bad romance novel, not a poem. There were no passages that made me want to stop and underline, there were only great globs of writing I wanted to stop and draw a line through. Truly the worst novel I've read this year if only because of its pretensions. Throw in the rest, and it's bad on a scale I haven't encountered in a long time. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16997123719356770551" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Stephanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/412317-stephanie"><img alt="Stephanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307761518p2/412317.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/8084792?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8084792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8223485514586227504">I have sort of a love-hate relationship with Jodi Picoult books. I really enjoyed Plain Truth and My Sister's Keeper, but there are definitely things about her writing that irritate me. It seems they were more apparent in this one. I personally think metaphors would be more effective (and part of a beautiful written piece) if they are few and really well woven into the book. In Vanishing Acts, Picoult tended to bash the reader over the head with meaningfulness and metaphorical irony. <br/>So basicall</span>
  <span id="freeText8223485514586227504" style="display:none">I have sort of a love-hate relationship with Jodi Picoult books. I really enjoyed Plain Truth and My Sister's Keeper, but there are definitely things about her writing that irritate me. It seems they were more apparent in this one. I personally think metaphors would be more effective (and part of a beautiful written piece) if they are few and really well woven into the book. In Vanishing Acts, Picoult tended to bash the reader over the head with meaningfulness and metaphorical irony. <br />So basically, if you've read and liked other Picoult books, read this one too. But if you've never read one of her books, start with a much better one (Plain Truth is my favorite) and only get to this one if you really like it.</span>

<div id="review_2202713" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2202713" />
    <a title="Michele" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/142538-michele"><img alt="Michele" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1182368778p2/142538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2202713?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michele" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michele" href="/user/show/142538-michele">Michele</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2202713" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16221909944376632372"><b>"The Only Way Someone Can Leave You Is If You Let Them."</b><br/>	<br/><i>Vanishing Acts</i> is yet another well told tale by Jodi Picoult, who is a master at character development. Once again telling the story through first person accounts of the main characters, she weaves together a family drama centered on a "kidnapping" that had occurred 28 years earlier.<br/><br/>Thirty-one year old Delia Hopkins, aka Bethany Matthews, discovers her loving and devoted father, took her away from her alcoholic mother and her childhood in </span>
  <span id="freeText16221909944376632372" style="display:none"><b>"The Only Way Someone Can Leave You Is If You Let Them."</b><br />	<br /><i>Vanishing Acts</i> is yet another well told tale by Jodi Picoult, who is a master at character development. Once again telling the story through first person accounts of the main characters, she weaves together a family drama centered on a "kidnapping" that had occurred 28 years earlier.<br /><br />Thirty-one year old Delia Hopkins, aka Bethany Matthews, discovers her loving and devoted father, took her away from her alcoholic mother and her childhood in Scottsdale, AZ, created new identities for himself and his daughter, and raised her on lies in New Hampshire. Delia believed her mother was killed in a car accident. When her father is arrested for the crime and put on trial back in Arizona, everything Delia knows to be true about her life and her world unravels.<br /><br />This is a quick and easy read. Through Delia, who for a living works with a bloodhound named "Greta" to track and find missing people, we experience the irony of her chosen occupation. Through her fiance, Eric, an alcoholic and the lawyer who defends Delia's father, we get a close up look at how alcoholism can destroy/alter so many families. Through Andrew Hopkins, aka Charlie Matthews, we get an insider's look at life in prison and learn to understand the desperation of a loving father. Other pertinent characters include Fitz, the best friend of both Delia and Eric, Sophie, Delia and Eric's young daughter, and Ruthanne, a Native American woman Delia and Sophie meet in a trailer park, where they temporarily reside in Arizona during the trial.<br /><br />Fans of Picoult will not be disappointed. I recommend this book for readers who look for good writing and interesting, dramatic story lines. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16221909944376632372" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/235200-elizabeth?shelf=listened-to-audio-version">listened-to-audio-version</a>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer9578396067845064069">I have been working my way through <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7128.Jodi_Picoult' title='Jodi Picoult' rel='nofollow noopener'> Jodi Picoult</a>'s books for the last couple of weeks and was really disappointed by this book.   <span id="freeText9578396067845064069" style="display:none">I have been working my way through <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7128.Jodi_Picoult" title="Jodi Picoult" rel="nofollow noopener"> Jodi Picoult</a>'s books for the last couple of weeks and was really disappointed by this book. I had previously read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10917.My_Sister_s_Keeper" title="My Sister's Keeper by Jodi Picoult" rel="nofollow noopener"> My Sister's Keeper</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10916.The_Pact" title="The Pact by Jodi Picoult" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Pact</a> and although I didn't love them I thought they were very well written and the multiple character angle worked in them. My main problem with this book was that there was too much going on, from start to finish there were just too many story lines (I felt the relationship between Delia, Erik and Fitz was pointless and was really disappointed in the outcome at the end of the book) and characters to keep track of (all of Andrew's jail mates and the Hopi people added unnecessary confusing trying to keep everyone straight). The final surprise at the end of the book was almost an after though (although the basis of it was introduced early in the book) and although it served a purpose I think it was too easy of an out.</span>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">Current Jodi Picoult die hard fans, my Mom</span></div>

    <span class="greyText">Recommended to ╟ ♫ Tima ♪ ╣ ♥ by: </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1236721427261255281"><b>Page 70, review:</b> I've just barely cracked into this book but I already needed to comment on something. I really dislike Picoult's use of different fonts for each character. (she does the same in <i>My Sister's Keeper</i> If you cannot write a character well enough that it can't stand alone in generic font..you ought to start writing from one perspective only. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3541.Barbara_Kingsolver' title='Barbara Kingsolver' rel='nofollow noopener'>Barbara Kingsolver</a> writes almost all her novels from the view of 3-4 different people per story and keeps the same font. She gives them such dept</span>
  <span id="freeText1236721427261255281" style="display:none"><b>Page 70, review:</b> I've just barely cracked into this book but I already needed to comment on something. I really dislike Picoult's use of different fonts for each character. (she does the same in <i>My Sister's Keeper</i> If you cannot write a character well enough that it can't stand alone in generic font..you ought to start writing from one perspective only. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3541.Barbara_Kingsolver" title="Barbara Kingsolver" rel="nofollow noopener">Barbara Kingsolver</a> writes almost all her novels from the view of 3-4 different people per story and keeps the same font. She gives them such depth and voice that they are entirely identifiable, no matter the font they're in. <br /><br /><b>Page 214, review:</b> Qualms #2 &amp; #3 about this book. I really am disliking the inconsistent perspectives the characters are using. Some of the characters are narrating in 1st person and some are narrating in 2nd person. There's one [the father] who switches between the two of them. It's making me want to smash the book in the garbage disposal. Qualm 3 is that this book is just a bit ridiculous, I'd love to give a full example of why, but i'm not ready to set up my spoiler tags yet.. oi vey! <br /><br /><b>Page 300, review:</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This book is getting increasingly more difficult to finish reading. I'm tiring of the jail chapters, the page long poorly written "raps from the courtyard", the entire meth operation with the father is just coming across really flimsy, unnecessary and highly uncharacteristic of the character Picoult has built - I just think she went too far over-board with this book. That seems to be the name of her game though, over-doing it. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br /><b>Final Review:</b> This book was pretty bad. It started out strong, interesting plot. Then gave way to a boring, predictable love triangle, a random section involving the Hopi Indians that seemed really out of place in the story and really awful decision with the father's story line. Truth be told, I skipped the last 100 pages and read the final chapter, amazing that I still knew exactly what had happened and didn't have to page backwards for clarifications. I thought the character development was sub-par and if she cut this book in half, it probably would've been a decent novel.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10031086022031050487">I have a slight love/hate relationship with Jodi Picoult novels. There have been a couple which I absolutely adored and several more that I didn't enjoy at all. This latest read falls firmly somewhere in the middle. <br/><br/>I enjoyed the initial plot outline, it was something different and I felt empathy for the lead characters. By midway, I was beginning to feel a little bored as I knew where the story was heading. The writing felt dated. By the time the grand court case that Picoult is famous for came</span>
  <span id="freeText10031086022031050487" style="display:none">I have a slight love/hate relationship with Jodi Picoult novels. There have been a couple which I absolutely adored and several more that I didn't enjoy at all. This latest read falls firmly somewhere in the middle. <br /><br />I enjoyed the initial plot outline, it was something different and I felt empathy for the lead characters. By midway, I was beginning to feel a little bored as I knew where the story was heading. The writing felt dated. By the time the grand court case that Picoult is famous for came to be, I had lost ninety percent of my patience with the book and found myself skimming the long court based conversations.<br /><br />Indeed some of the characters are interesting but too many of their actions felt contrived. As so many of this authors books focus on similar topics, she needs to ensure that every single one is brilliant. This was just about okay. To date, her best book has been The Storyteller. <br /><br />On a final note, this book signifies my 100th read in 2016, reaching my target. With still several weeks of the year to go, I hope to exceed my initial target by tackling several more books on my ever growing to read list. </span>

<div id="review_1464218270" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1464218270" />
    <a title="Laila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9908703-laila"><img alt="Laila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442654021p2/9908703.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1464218270?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laila" href="/user/show/9908703-laila">Laila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9908703-laila?shelf=genre-contemporary-lit">genre-contemporary-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9908703-laila?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1464218270" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5747608827691429427">I've read better from her. It wasn't terrible and I enjoyed parts of it, but all in all there were too many issues that bothered me and left me with an odd feeling. Partly, and I've had the same issue with some of her other books, especially my sister's keeper, where I feel like my idea of poetic justice or how people feel and react are just SLIGHTLY off hers. Which is worse than completely off, somehow.<br/><br/>Mostly I feel like she crammed a few too many side-plots and characters into this.<br/>- I really </span>
  <span id="freeText5747608827691429427" style="display:none">I've read better from her. It wasn't terrible and I enjoyed parts of it, but all in all there were too many issues that bothered me and left me with an odd feeling. Partly, and I've had the same issue with some of her other books, especially my sister's keeper, where I feel like my idea of poetic justice or how people feel and react are just SLIGHTLY off hers. Which is worse than completely off, somehow.<br /><br />Mostly I feel like she crammed a few too many side-plots and characters into this.<br />- I really could have done without the love triangle or Fitz the character (whiny, useless, zero agency in the story)<br />- Same with her mother's santaria. While I liked the Native American subplot (I'm no expert in how it was handled) because it really factored into the story and led to insights the MC needed, her mother's witchcraft was just this loose thread that never tied back into the plot.<br />- Same with the Orange-is-the-new-Black stuff with Andrew in prison. I get that it showed how he can become a criminal when pushed into it, but the elements just seemed jangled and weird and it kept ripping me out of the story. And the worst: it has ZERO impact on the story or the main character. It's just gruesome stuff that happens to him, while he can brag (like Piper in Oitnb) that he is the ONLY white non-racist ever to enter prison *yawn*. <br /><br />And I never say this, but OMG the "big secret" was so effing obvious it hurt how stupid and blind all the characters were. I really don't mind being able to figure out how things end, that's fine with me, but when the clues are so obvious and none of the characters react to it at all... yeah. Not good.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[1. There is literally ONE obvious reason to steal a child in that situation. One. Sexual abuse or other abuse that can't be proven. So you already start out thinking it has to be that in the end.<br />2. Andrew is very, very transparent.<br />3. The guy actually took her daughter BY HIMSELF, WITHOUT the mother's okay, after they had seen each other like twice. THAT'S NOT NORMAL. And she actually thanks him, and thinks that's totally fine... what?! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Finally... the ending. <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I know this is subjective, but I really hated the MC for the way she ended up treating Eric. And this makes me extra mad, because I usually feel like female MCs are subject to crazy scrutiny in a way make MCs are not, and I try not to do that, but OMG I can't help it in this case.<br />Throughout the book, I went on and off her (like most of the characters). First I was CRAZY annoyed at all the dudes who treat her like some fragile thing who can't handle anything and therefore has to be lied to and has NO right to her own truth and her own story. Which is bullshit. But then whenever she is told things, she reacts in ways that makes me think I'd probably end up lying too.<br />[Also I am getting increasingly annoyed by the amount of fictional characters who seem to think that nobody should ever lie and if you catch someone in a lie that means you can never trust anything again! *DRAMA* - EVERYBODY lies. Parents lie all the time. Kids lie. Teachers lie. Friends lie. Partners lie. Get over it.]<br />And then the ending. Eric starts drinking again (a little bit, no wife-beating, child-endangering, pass-out in a bar kind of drinking) because she puts the most incredible pressure on him imaginable. (Dude, they could have just hired a lawyer, if she cared about him and his sobriety and then helped the lawyer). And then when he cracks under unimaginable pressure, she tells him "I can't carry your baggage" -- which I'm sorry, but that's kinda what you do when you love someone. Not without limits, not by enabling him, but he has just spent months carrying her massive mountain of baggage. And he deserves her help. That just didn't seem fair. Especially when, as someone who loves an alcoholic, you should know more about it and not actively put him in a position that he probably can't handle... only to then make it worse and worse and worse throughout the book, by being really selfish.<br />Also omg, how could she go to Fitz? He is SO boring and in my reading of it, they had ZERO chemistry. All the way to there, I was going to write that Picoult does this amazing thing, where you can FEEL the love and intimacy between two people so intensely, especially by contrasting it to the complete lack of it with Fitz. NONE. <br />But then, full disclosure, that might have been in part because I listened to the audiobook and the reader for Fitz had a really boyish, whiny voice...But his character just sucked. His one personality trait was being a passive "nice guy" who spends his life in the "friendzone" waiting for his big chance. I hate guys like that. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="5747608827691429427" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_6731952" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6731952" />
    <a title="Liza" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/278098-liza"><img alt="Liza" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1187139385p2/278098.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6731952?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liza" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liza" href="/user/show/278098-liza">Liza</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6731952" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer220513096963575352">I'm in a Piccoult zone. THis is the second book of hers that I've read and I"ve just started a new one. I appreciate the depth of the topics she writes about, this one, the ethics of a father's decision to kidnap his daughter from a staggering, alcoholic mother. Was the daughter better off never knowing her mother? Was losing her daughter what the mother needed to get clean, the ultimate tough love test? Did the father have the right to make that decision for everyone based on his fears and disc</span>
  <span id="freeText220513096963575352" style="display:none">I'm in a Piccoult zone. THis is the second book of hers that I've read and I"ve just started a new one. I appreciate the depth of the topics she writes about, this one, the ethics of a father's decision to kidnap his daughter from a staggering, alcoholic mother. Was the daughter better off never knowing her mother? Was losing her daughter what the mother needed to get clean, the ultimate tough love test? Did the father have the right to make that decision for everyone based on his fears and discomforts in the situation? Were there other alternatives for a man, a single father, in the seventies? <br /><br />Fact is, this is a very real situation that deserves very real attention. I think Jodi Piccoult touched on some of the more elusive elements of situations like these, and touched on them well. <br /><br />So far, two books into her collection, I am very impressed. </span>
  <a data-text-id="220513096963575352" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Holly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Holly" href="/user/show/826221-holly">Holly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781419320149" href="/book/show/255250.Vanishing_Acts">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/826221-holly?shelf=recorded-book">recorded-book</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer18089517&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18089517" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3307341453220388364">I either liked this one four stars or two, depending on the part I'm thinking of. As always, Jodi Picoult handles astonishing emotional situations and provides plenty to care and think about when a grown woman learns she was abducted as a child--by her kind and nurturing father.<br/><br/>The rest of the story centers around the characters and the ensuing legal drama. It is heavily a story about motherhood and expectations, with a realistic angle on alcholism thrown in for good measure.<br/><br/>Two things that real</span>
  <span id="freeText3307341453220388364" style="display:none">I either liked this one four stars or two, depending on the part I'm thinking of. As always, Jodi Picoult handles astonishing emotional situations and provides plenty to care and think about when a grown woman learns she was abducted as a child--by her kind and nurturing father.<br /><br />The rest of the story centers around the characters and the ensuing legal drama. It is heavily a story about motherhood and expectations, with a realistic angle on alcholism thrown in for good measure.<br /><br />Two things that really bothered me: There was one character I grew attached to who seemed to serve no real purpose except to give the protagonist a reason to bring out her search and rescue dog, because how cool is that, that an abducted child grows up to do search and rescue?<br /><br />The other element I didn't care for, and never do no matter how many times I encounter it, is the protagonist who has a willingly spare lover on the hook for when the other relationship doesn't work out, like an emergency ration. This is obviously a matter of personal taste, and Picoult is the first author I've seen use this plot element and not wreck the entire story with it...maybe because her story is superior to begin with.<br /><br />Besides Picoult's style and voice, other pluses include the settings--especially the jail scenes from the kidnapper father's point of view. The killer triple twist at the end made me glad I'd stuck with it, and a healthy dose of moral ambiguity ensure I'm going to remember this story for a very long time. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3307341453220388364" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText18027504733226514908" style="display:none">4.5*<br /><br />The whole finding out you were kidnapped as a child premise interests me every time. <div id="review_49815552" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer49815552" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9370386263491788540">When I reached the halfway point of this 418 page book, I found myself wishing that I could just put it down and be done with it; but since I'd made it that far, I made the commitment to trudge on through to the end. Was it worth it? Only in the sense that, having completed it, I can now add it to my "Read in 2012" list. My 3-star rating means that it was just average for me; it wasn't horrible, but it wasn't any better than "okay", either. It even bordered on being annoying. By that description</span>
  <span id="freeText9370386263491788540" style="display:none">When I reached the halfway point of this 418 page book, I found myself wishing that I could just put it down and be done with it; but since I'd made it that far, I made the commitment to trudge on through to the end. Was it worth it? Only in the sense that, having completed it, I can now add it to my "Read in 2012" list. My 3-star rating means that it was just average for me; it wasn't horrible, but it wasn't any better than "okay", either. It even bordered on being annoying. By that description, I should probably give it a 2, but I'll stick with my pattern of "rounding up" with my ratings.<br /><br />One problem I had with it was that I didn't particularly like any of the characters. Everyone seemed to think that everything was all about Delia, and that protecting her feelings and making her happy were all that mattered in the world. Just annoying. As for Delia herself, I didn't really like her either. She came across as self-centered, although I guess it'd be hard <i>not</i> to be when everyone around you constantly dotes on you. In addition, there was a scene in which an animal was killed (this is not a spoiler) and she didn't even blink twice. I can't respect anyone, real or fictional, who wouldn't get upset in that scenario. <br /><br />Another major problem I had with the book was how all the characters were constantly having these tangential thoughts in the middle of any given situation; it broke up the story and made it just draaaaag along. Worse, these thoughts were supposed to be all deep and profound, but really were not.<br /><br />Then there was the font! Each chapter was a first-person point of view of a different character (alternating between Delia, her dad, her fiance, and her best friend) - and a different font was used for each character. This was unnecessary and distracting. You get used to reading a certain font, and then when it abruptly changes, it takes some getting used to again. <br /><br />Lastly, the story was just boring. Feeling no great connection to any of the characters, I would have at least liked a little action, but it wasn't an action-driven novel. Nor did I find it suspenseful or intriguing. There was the typical "twist" at the end, but by that time, I just didn't really even care. <br /><br />I've read 3 books by Jodi Picoult now, and liked each one progressively less than the one I read before it. I'll give her one or two more tries, but unless I like them a whole lot better than this one, I'll give her up entirely. <br /><br />ETA: On second thought, I went back and changed my rating to 2 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9370386263491788540" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1288745878" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1288745878" />
    <a title="Suzanne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12466067-suzanne"><img alt="Suzanne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498789036p2/12466067.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1288745878?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suzanne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suzanne" href="/user/show/12466067-suzanne">Suzanne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12466067-suzanne?shelf=mixed-reviews">mixed-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1288745878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13172258280218023367">I'm in two minds about Vanishing Acts. When I first started it, I was immediately excited by how the story drew me in, and pleased with Picoult’s command of writing, and I thought to myself, this is going to be a good book. For a good portion of the story, JP’s writing riveted me, but the story took a detour down a long winding trail that got a bit lumpy along the way. <br/><br/>For me, the problem was Picoult seemed to have thrown everything — and the kitchen sink — into this book. Subplots popped up lik</span>
  <span id="freeText13172258280218023367" style="display:none">I'm in two minds about Vanishing Acts. When I first started it, I was immediately excited by how the story drew me in, and pleased with Picoult’s command of writing, and I thought to myself, this is going to be a good book. For a good portion of the story, JP’s writing riveted me, but the story took a detour down a long winding trail that got a bit lumpy along the way. <br /><br />For me, the problem was Picoult seemed to have thrown everything — and the kitchen sink — into this book. Subplots popped up like dandelions, leaving a bitter taste in my mouth. I suspect JP didn’t have a place for all the things she wanted to write, and convinced herself she could put them into this book though the story didn’t actually call for them, and might have been a smoother read without. <br /><br />Case in point: Andrew’s s stint in prison. Reading his POV about the rules of prison, the fights, the nicknames of the other inmates, I began to wonder why JP was telling us all this. I figured there <i>must</i> be a reason, so I held on, reading the exhaustive descriptions of the prison and it’s inmates, the silly poem and the rap song circulating about D-block, even the Breaking Bad chapter where Walter White-like chemist, Andrew, becomes a meth cooker. <br /><br />What was the reason? Got me. <br /><br />Ruthann and the Hopi Indian storyline was slightly interesting … the repurposed Barbies made me laugh, but again, JP became a bit indulgent by making us visit the reservation and witness Ruthann’s cliff diving. Why? I don't know.<br /><br />Maybe JP was trying to draw out a special meaning with the Indian and prison chapters. Regrettably, I didn’t connect the relevance to the story.<br /><br />I really loved the story of three friends, Eric, Fritz and Delia. I liked learning about how they grew up together, and how their emotional feelings seesawed, and yet, their devotion to each other never faltered. I didn’t love Delia’s character (she was always shutting down and running away when things got tough), but she was okay, and I felt for her problem. <br /><br />I connected with both of the guys, particularly Eric. He was probably my favorite character because he was so fallible, but he knew it. I thought it was brilliant for JP to put Eric into the plot like she did, paralleling his drinking problem to his defense case. I understood Fritz unrequited love for Delia, but I was not thrilled with where the story went concerning those two. There were a great many questions left unanswered at the end, and I would have liked more closure, perhaps an epilogue, telling us what happens to the three of them… where do they end up, and with whom?<br /><br />JP is really good at taking commonplace opinions and turning things upside down and make you look at it in a whole new way. There were lots of elements in the book that makes ones think, but what sticks in my head is the thread about memory; how much do we really retain and how much is actually subjective.<br /><br />Vanishing Acts is not one of favorites by Picoult, but by no means would I hesitate to read more by her. She is a talented writer.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13172258280218023367" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_104098457" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/104098457" />
    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3771119-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1332015028p2/3771119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/104098457?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/3771119-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3771119-julie?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3771119-julie?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer104098457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2087279859577966373">This is a pretty formulaic Picoult book. She tackles many issues in this book including kidnapping, alcoholism, memory, being a parent, etc. The novel is told from multiple perspectives: Delia, who finds out her father kidnapped her as a four-year-old; Eric, Delia’s alcoholic fiancé who happens to be a lawyer and defends her father; Andrew, Delia’s father who spends a majority of the novel in jail; Fitz, Eric and Delia’s best friend; and Elise, Delia’s mother who has not seen her daughter in twe</span>
  <span id="freeText2087279859577966373" style="display:none">This is a pretty formulaic Picoult book. She tackles many issues in this book including kidnapping, alcoholism, memory, being a parent, etc. The novel is told from multiple perspectives: Delia, who finds out her father kidnapped her as a four-year-old; Eric, Delia’s alcoholic fiancé who happens to be a lawyer and defends her father; Andrew, Delia’s father who spends a majority of the novel in jail; Fitz, Eric and Delia’s best friend; and Elise, Delia’s mother who has not seen her daughter in twenty-eight years. In true Picoult fashion, the sequence of events plays itself out: Andrew gets arrested and sent to Arizona to await trial, Delia, Eric, and their daughter relocate there temporarily, Fitz tags along and creates friction, Delia meets her mother, whom she thought was dead, and a trial begins, with Eric as the defense attorney. <br /><br />Like all of Jodi’s books, I was captivated and got though Vanishing Acts very quickly. It wasn’t quite as engaging as some of her others, but I still enjoyed it. The one aspect I can say she could have done without was Andrew’s narrative from jail. I understand the need to convey what a deplorable situation he was in, but I found it hard to believe that a sixty-year-old man would willingly engage in crime so freely with his fellow prisoners, even being a party to their Crystal Meth smuggling schemes. I liked the change of scenery in this book. For once, Picoult takes the reader outside of New England into a somewhat mystical Southwest. The conclusion left a few mysteries, but led the reader to form their own conclusions in regard to the truth. This is a book that any Jodi fan will enjoy.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2087279859577966373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I think that those people are haters! <br />1.people did not like that she switched characters and fonts,<br />I say why not!?? like they have never read a book that has done that???<br />2. people did not like that she had unnessasary characters and sub-plots, don't all large novels have those??? <div id="review_11345919" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/11345919" />
    <a title="Rachel Baird " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/729332-rachel-baird"><img alt="Rachel Baird " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1199133419p2/729332.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer16663344079158523560">this was my 2nd jodi picoult. i hadn't been so thoroughly engrossed in a book in quite some time. its a quick and enjoyable read that will make you laugh, cry, and keep you on the edge of your seat the whole time. i love the way picoult questions morally complicated situations. the plot was one of the most interesting ideas i have every read and i found myself emotionally, intellectually, and morally challenged throughout my reading. <br/><br/>i have heard complaints about the way jodi picoult does not ma</span>
  <span id="freeText16663344079158523560" style="display:none">this was my 2nd jodi picoult. i hadn't been so thoroughly engrossed in a book in quite some time. its a quick and enjoyable read that will make you laugh, cry, and keep you on the edge of your seat the whole time. i love the way picoult questions morally complicated situations. the plot was one of the most interesting ideas i have every read and i found myself emotionally, intellectually, and morally challenged throughout my reading. <br /><br />i have heard complaints about the way jodi picoult does not make clear who is right and who is wrong and that she doesn't answer all the questions posed by her works, but that is what i love about her. that is life. things aren't black and white, situations are messy and muddled and well-meaning people may do bad things. </span>

<div id="review_140882662" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/140882662" />
    <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions"><img alt="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464118116p2/2602702.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/140882662?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions">Christina (A Reader of Fictions)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer140882662" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16702870731308799463">Jodi Picoult is one of the most popular contemporary authors. I have read and enjoyed (to varying degrees) three of her other novels. For one of my classes at Pitt, we read My Sister's Keeper, or were supposed to. I had read the book prior to taking the course and did not reread it. That one was my favorite of the Picoult books I had read. Imagine my surprise when all of my friends hated it. They said the writing was absolutely atrocious.<br/><br/>In my reading of Vanishing Acts, I paid way more attention</span>
  <span id="freeText16702870731308799463" style="display:none">Jodi Picoult is one of the most popular contemporary authors. I have read and enjoyed (to varying degrees) three of her other novels. For one of my classes at Pitt, we read My Sister's Keeper, or were supposed to. I had read the book prior to taking the course and did not reread it. That one was my favorite of the Picoult books I had read. Imagine my surprise when all of my friends hated it. They said the writing was absolutely atrocious.<br /><br />In my reading of Vanishing Acts, I paid way more attention to the construction of the novel than I ordinarily do on a first time through a book (in which, unless the story is absolutely awful, I focus on the plot and the characters). I still thought the story itself was engaging, but I definitely found weaknesses in the characterization/writing. The main problem is that, if the fonts were not different for each character, I would constantly have been forgetting which character's point of view I was currently reading. They lack a unique voice. And even when they were freaked out about something, they all continued to read as a bit disaffected.<br /><br />Although changing the font for each different character is neat, I really think you ought to be able to tell which character is 'speaking' without needing that. Or even without a heading. Also, I have to admit that I was annoyed by the similarity between Andrew's (Delia's father) and Eric's (Delia's fiancee) fonts. Is Picoult (or the publisher) trying to suggest that Delia has serious Elektra complex type daddy issues? Or were they just too lazy to find another font that looked entirely different from the others? There are thousands of fonts; how hard can it be?<br /><br />All three had two things in common, despite their differing plots: a focus on family and a twist at the very end. The twist here was...pretty much nonexistent. The only things that could maybe called twists are Delia's continual rediscoveries of memories and a 'revelation' that was completely unsurprising given the discourse of the previous chapters.<br /><br />A decent read on an interesting subject, but not an astounding book. Now for some lyrics! (This song was also selected because alcoholism is a huge topic in this book; about half of the characters are, were or were related to alcoholics).</span>
  <a data-text-id="16702870731308799463" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_5213485" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/5213485" />
    <a title="Cecilia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/300260-cecilia"><img alt="Cecilia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1187806571p2/300260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/5213485?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cecilia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cecilia" href="/user/show/300260-cecilia">Cecilia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer5213485" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3994273644617994778">I have decided to create a new genre of fiction: Missing Child Fiction. This category will include such titles as The Lovely Bones by Alice Seybold, The Little Friend by Donna Tartt, How to Be Lost by Amanda Eyre Ward, The Bright Forever by Lee Martin, and this book, Vanishing Acts by Jodi Picoult.<br/><br/>Having recently read so many books with plots that revolve around a missing child I began to consider what about this topic inspires so much powerful fiction and compels so many of us to read these boo</span>
  <span id="freeText3994273644617994778" style="display:none">I have decided to create a new genre of fiction: Missing Child Fiction. This category will include such titles as The Lovely Bones by Alice Seybold, The Little Friend by Donna Tartt, How to Be Lost by Amanda Eyre Ward, The Bright Forever by Lee Martin, and this book, Vanishing Acts by Jodi Picoult.<br /><br />Having recently read so many books with plots that revolve around a missing child I began to consider what about this topic inspires so much powerful fiction and compels so many of us to read these books. Perhaps we believe that by reading about the unthinkable – the disappearance of a child we love – we can avoid it in reality, or perhaps we become more grateful for the safety of the children in our lives. Regardless of the psychology behind this type of book, the aforementioned ones are all well told, well written, compelling fiction.<br /><br />Vanishing Acts is the story of a woman who finds out as an adult that her father, who raised her, had kidnapped her away from her alcoholic mother, who she thought was dead. The story examines this event in the context of what is legal versus what is right. It also examines alcoholism from the perspective of both alcoholics and those who love them. As with all of Picoult’s novels, it fairly examines a difficult moral issue and causes the reader to do the same. The story is told through different character’s voices, and each character has their own narrator in this audiobook version. All the narrators do solid work, though some stand out more than others. This is my favorite of Picoult’s novels, and I strongly recommend it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3994273644617994778" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1997126487" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1997126487" />
    <a title="Jessica Ashe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9511730-jessica-ashe"><img alt="Jessica Ashe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481891673p2/9511730.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1997126487?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica Ashe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica Ashe" href="/user/show/9511730-jessica-ashe">Jessica Ashe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9511730-jessica-ashe?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1997126487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6880696640223005516">Mysterious & terrifying until the very end<br/><br/><br/>Who was your favorite character and why?<br/>I loved the father. He lied, cheated & stole for what was in the best interest of his daughter, the mark of a true parent in my opinion. He was willing to go to any length to ensure that his daughter was safe from her mother and her boyfriend.<br/><br/>Did you have an extreme reaction to this book? Did it make you laugh or cry?<br/>I must say, this book did cause me to shed a few tears, mainly because for me it hits very close to</span>
  <span id="freeText6880696640223005516" style="display:none">Mysterious &amp; terrifying until the very end<br /><br /><br />Who was your favorite character and why?<br />I loved the father. He lied, cheated &amp; stole for what was in the best interest of his daughter, the mark of a true parent in my opinion. He was willing to go to any length to ensure that his daughter was safe from her mother and her boyfriend.<br /><br />Did you have an extreme reaction to this book? Did it make you laugh or cry?<br />I must say, this book did cause me to shed a few tears, mainly because for me it hits very close to home. In my own childhood, my mother was an alcoholic &amp; drug addict. I can recall coming home from school not being able to wake her, not knowing if she was just drunk or if I should call 911. My own mother would take us to her dealers houses in the middle of the night, not concerned with if we had school the following day or if she was putting us in harms way. In this sense, I identify with this book. <br /><br />The repressed memories are a very interesting subject that I look forward to learning more about, but also in a way, it is terrifying to think you could learn something that you may not want to know.<br /><br />To this day, my mother is a drug addict and alcoholic and even though I have forgiven her, I have no desire to forge a relationship with her. It's a strange feeling to know that you should have feelings for someone as special as your mother who should have walked to the edges of the earth for you, and yet feel the same as if you were passing a stranger on the street of a busy street.<br /><br />The ending of this book really threw me for a loop. During the last 5 minutes, you are sure you see how this is playing out and at the very end you find out exactly why the father took his little girl away from her mother. <br /><br />Sometimes it's vital to take heed to those gut feelings.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6880696640223005516" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2863044304" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2863044304" />
    <a title="Randy Tramp" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21953550-randy-tramp"><img alt="Randy Tramp" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1429295868p2/21953550.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2863044304?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Randy Tramp" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Randy Tramp" href="/user/show/21953550-randy-tramp">Randy Tramp</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2863044304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14054758333214695539">Delia Hopkins lives in rural New Hampshire. She has a young daughter, Sophia, a fiance Eric, and her own search-and-rescue bloodhound, which she uses to find missing persons.<br/><br/>The first chapter drew me in. Hints of something not right sprinkled on the pages. Then the reveal at the end of chapter one: a policeman knocks on Delia's door revealing a secret that changes her world.<br/><br/>I love Jodi's writing style. First person with each character's name at the beginning of each chapter, giving several point</span>
  <span id="freeText14054758333214695539" style="display:none">Delia Hopkins lives in rural New Hampshire. She has a young daughter, Sophia, a fiance Eric, and her own search-and-rescue bloodhound, which she uses to find missing persons.<br /><br />The first chapter drew me in. Hints of something not right sprinkled on the pages. Then the reveal at the end of chapter one: a policeman knocks on Delia's door revealing a secret that changes her world.<br /><br />I love Jodi's writing style. First person with each character's name at the beginning of each chapter, giving several points of view. I find myself reading through one chapter so I could see what the next person is thinking.<br /><br />Each character has their own set of problems. Identity is the theme of this book. Who am I? Each character struggles with that question. Andrew, the father, has to go through much to get to the point of finding that answer. Delia seeks to recover memory like finding pieces of a puzzle.<br /><br />Picoult has a way of writing novels that cause you to deep think. This book will remain with me for a long time.<br /><br />Rating: Some curse words. A few sexual scenes. Violence inside a prison.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14054758333214695539" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
